- **x-part is \(x e^{-|x|}\)** (odd, non-polynomial, non-piecewise-linear), and **no constant term**, no \(x^2,x^3,\dots\), no trig, no logs.

Below, each candidate is checked for whether its function class can be made identical to \( -0.5995\,v - 2.7952\,x e^{-|x|}\) on some plausible continuous domain (e.g., \(x\ge 0\) or \(x\le 0\), \(v\ge 0\), etc.) by choosing constants.

### 1
Polynomial/Max in \(v\) plus polynomial in \(x\) (includes \(x, x|x|, x^3, x^5\)). No \(e^{-|x|}\). Cannot equal \(x e^{-|x|}\) on any open interval. **No.**

### 30
Has \(\exp(c7 x)\) as a standalone term, but GT needs \(x e^{-|x|}\) (odd, vanishes at 0). A standalone \(\exp(c7 x)\) cannot equal \(x e^{-|x|}\) on any open interval. Also includes polynomials. **No.**

### 31
Has \(\log(c7 e^{c8 x}+1)\) term; cannot become \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 32
Has \(x\exp(c9 x^2)\) (this is \(x e^{c9 x^2}\), even exponent in \(x\)), whereas GT is \(x e^{-|x|}\) (linear absolute in exponent). No choice of constants makes \(e^{c9 x^2}\equiv e^{-|x|}\) on an interval. Also extra \(v\)-dependent exponentials. **No.**

### 33
Has \(e^{c3 x}\) (no \(|x|\)) and \(v|v|\). Cannot match. **No.**

### 34
Has \(e^{c3 x}\) and \(v e^{c7 x}\); wrong structure. **No.**

### 35
Has \(v e^{c5 x}\) and \(x^{c8} e^{c9 x}\). Could we set \(c8=1\) and \(c9=-1\) to get \(x e^{-x}\)? Yes, but GT needs \(x e^{-|x|}\). Conditional domain \(x\ge 0\) would make \(|x|=x\), so GT’s x-part becomes \(x e^{-x}\) on \(x\ge 0\). However candidate’s term is \(c7 x^{c8} e^{c9 x}\) **plus** unavoidable polynomial terms \(c0 x^3 + c1 x^2 + c2 x + c3 + c6 x^5\) which must be set to 0 (possible). Then we’d have \(c7 x e^{-x}\) which can match \(-2.7952 x e^{-x}\) by \(c7=-2.79522534599104\).  
But candidate still has \(c4 v e^{c5 x}\). To match GT’s \(-0.5995 v\) (no \(x\) dependence), we would need \(c5=0\) so \(e^{c5 x}=1\), and set \(c4=-0.59954989233168\). That seems workable.  
**Problem:** candidate’s exponential in x is \(e^{c9 x}\) (no absolute), so equivalence holds only on domain \(x\ge 0\) (or \(x\le 0\) with different sign). That is allowed.  
So **(35) CAN match GT on domain \(x\ge 0\)** with:
- \(c0=c1=c2=c3=c6=0\)
- \(c5=0,\; c4=-0.59954989233168\)
- \(c8=1,\; c9=-1,\; c7=-2.79522534599104\)

Thus (35) is a valid conditional match.

### 36
Has \(v e^{c5 x}\) and \(x^{c7} e^{c8 v}\) and \(v^3\). To get linear \(v\) only, must kill \(v^3\) and avoid \(e^{c8 v}\) dependence: set \(c9=0\) and \(c6=0\) (or \(c8=0\) makes \(e^{0}=1\) but still leaves \(x^{c7}\) term independent of \(v\) which could help). Yet there is **no \(e^{\pm x}\)** term independent of \(v\) unless we use \(x^{c7} e^{c8 v}\) with \(c8=0\) giving \(x^{c7}\) (polynomial/power), not \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 37
Similar to (36) with \(v|v|\). Cannot produce \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 38
Has \(\exp(c6\sin(c7 x+c8))\), not \(e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 39

### 40
Has \(v e^{c6|x|}\) and \(v|x|\) etc; exponential tied to \(v\). No standalone \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 41
Has \(v e^{c5 x}\) and \(x^{c7} e^{c8 v}\) plus linear \(v\). No way to get \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 42
Polynomial + piecewise in \(v\) + \(v x^2\). No \(e^{-|x|}\). **No.**

### 43
Has sine term; cannot become \(x e^{-|x|}\) on an interval (analytic mismatch). **No.**

### 44
Has \(v e^{c6|x|}\) tied to \(v\) and \(x^5\). No. **No.**

### 45

### 46
Polynomial + piecewise in \(v\) + \(v x^2\). No. **No.**

### 48

### 49

GT Equivalence Verification (PO19)

GT: -c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.59954989233168*v - 2.79522534599104*x*exp(-Abs(x))**

This is a function of `v` and `x` (no `t` dependence), with two terms:
1. A linear term in `v`
2. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` — this is NOT a polynomial in x, and NOT expressible as a finite combination of polynomials and `x*Abs(x)`.

Let me analyze the key function `x*exp(-Abs(x))`. The Taylor series of `exp(-|x|)` involves infinitely many terms, so `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be exactly represented by any finite polynomial in `x`, `|x|`, `x*|x|`, `x^3`, `x^5`, etc.

The critical question for each candidate is: **does it contain basis functions that can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-Abs(x))`?**

Let me categorize the candidates:

**Candidates with only polynomial/piecewise-polynomial terms in x and linear/polynomial terms in v** (e.g., `x`, `x²`, `x³`, `x⁵`, `x*Abs(x)`, `Max(0,v)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v³`):
These CANNOT match because `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is not a polynomial. This eliminates:
Candidates 1, 2, 5, 7, 8, 9, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 17, 18, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28, 42, 46, 48, 49, 50.

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*Abs(x))` terms** (3, 21, 40, 44): These have `v*exp(c*|x|)`, not `x*exp(-|x|)`. The `v` factor makes this fundamentally different from `x*exp(-|x|)`. NO MATCH.

**Candidates with `exp(c*x)` terms** (30, 31, 33, 34): `exp(c*x)` is not `exp(-|x|)` since `|x|` is not linear. NO MATCH.

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*x)` terms** (10, 20, 29, 35, 36, 37, 41): These have `v*exp(cx)`, not `x*exp(-|x|)`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 4**: Has `v*cos(c7*t)*Abs(x)` — setting c6=0 removes it, leaving polynomials. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 6**: `c7*x**3*exp(c7*v)` — this has `v` in the exponent, not `|x|`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 16**: `c7*exp(c8*Abs(x)**c9)` — This gives `exp(c8*|x|^c9)`. We need `x*exp(-|x|)`, but this term has no `x` multiplier outside. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 19**: `c7*v*exp(c8*Abs(v))` — depends on `v`, not `x`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 29, 35, 37, 36, 41, 45**: Various `x^c*exp(cv)` terms — wrong structure. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 32**: Has `x*exp(c9*x²)` — this is `x*exp(cx²)`, not `x*exp(-|x|)`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 38**: `exp(c6*sin(c7*x+c8))` — transcendental but wrong form. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 39**: `exp(c8*x)*exp(c9*v)` — wrong form. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 43**: `sin(c6*x+c7)` — trig, not exponential. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 47**: `exp(c7*v)*sin(c8*x*|x|+c9)` — wrong form. NO MATCH.

None of the candidates contain the basis function `x*exp(-|x|)` or any combination that could produce it exactly.
